         <tei:p>Due to their great size, individuals of this species must be particularly vulnerable to injury and<tei:lb/>liable to extinction in cultivation. The collection of specimens may prove increasingly difficult if<tei:lb/>not impossible in time, as more land is developed or ploughed for agriculture.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>REMARKS. A variable species particularly in the presence of, and patterns formed by, the papillae<tei:lb/>both in the pre-clitellar region and in the genital field. Most specimens examined have paired<tei:lb/>papillae on the pre-clitellar segments together with discrete male porophores but sometimes the<tei:lb/>pre-clitellar papillae are single, even mid- ventral, and the male porophores are joined by a trans-<tei:lb/>verse ridge. These latter variants are present among the series from the Bosumtwe area. The<tei:lb/>location of the caeca can be difficult to determine depending on the fixation techniques employed<tei:lb/>by the collector, but it does seem that sometimes the caeca do occur more posteriorly, perhaps as<tei:lb/>far back as segment xxvii.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Millsonia heteronephra (Michaelsen, 1897)<tei:lb/>(Figs9A&amp;10A)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Benhamia heteronephra Michaelsen, 1897: 22.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Dichogaster heteronephra: Michaelsen, 1900: 365.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>292 R. w. SIMS</tei:p>
         <tei:p>papillae in setal line a present in furrows 12/13-15/16; six or seven pairs of intestinal caeca<tei:lb/>xxvi-xxxi (xxxii); holo- and meronephric.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 251-336 mm, diameter 6-9 mm. Segments 518-580<tei:lb/>(? 600), multiannulate with a variable number of annuli anteriorly but triannulate behind the<tei:lb/>clitellum. First dorsal pore (10/11) 11/12. Clitellum (xiii) xiv-xix (xx), saddle-shaped extending<tei:lb/>ventrally to below setal line c but possibly to a anteriorly. Male pores paired jcvm, in mature<tei:lb/>individuals they are located in genital pits or pouches that in. preserved specimens may become<tei:lb/>everted; the pores can be seen above setal line d discharging into short lateral grooves that join<tei:lb/>paired longitudinal seminal grooves passing between inconspicuous paired prostatic pores in xvii<tei:lb/>and xix.          <tei:p>Internal characters. Septa 5/6-10/1 1 very thick, 11/12 less so. Gizzards unequal with the hinder<tei:lb/>being slightly larger and more strongly muscularized.          <tei:p>TYPE LOCALITY. Misahohe, Benim.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MATERIAL EXAMINED. Previously recorded. 1C (immature) 'Misahohe Station', Misahohe (659'N. 040'E.),</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Benim; coll. Ernst Baumann, 10 Nov. 1893; Hamburg V. 4520 (syntype of Benhamia heteronephra, other</tei:p>
         <tei:p>two syntypes originally reported, not found Zoologisches Institut und Zoologisches Museum, Universitat</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Hamburg, September 1982).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>New records. 2C (anterior fragments), 2A 1 juv. Maize plantation, Akoto Ambiente east of Bibiani (630'N.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>208'W.), near the road from Kumasi, southern Ghana; coll. J.D. Plisko, 8 Jun. 1966; BM(NH)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>1984.12.11-15.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DISTRIBUTION. Southern Benim and southern Ghana.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REMARKS. The outstanding feature of M. heteronephra is that the male genital field becomes grossly<tei:lb/>developed with the onset of sexual maturity when the male and prostatic pores are displaced<tei:lb/>laterally until the left and right sides of the field can be directly applied to the widely paired,<tei:lb/>laterally situated spermathecal pores of a partner during copulation. (The surviving syntype is<tei:lb/>immature and the male genital field is only poorly developed with the male and prostatic pores still<tei:lb/>located somewhat ventrally.)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>There is a discrepancy between the morphologies of the specimens described above and<tei:lb/>Michaelsen's original description. In the specimens examined from Ghana, the location of the<tei:lb/>intestinal caeca can be established with certainty between the segments xxvi-xxxi, whereas<tei:lb/>Michaelsen recorded their presence in xxxvi-xli, i.e. ten segments more posteriorly. (Although he<tei:lb/>recorded six pairs of caeca, he stated that seven pairs were present and, in 1900, he commented that<tei:lb/>there may be one or two pairs more.) Unfortunately, the anterior intestine with the caeca has been<tei:lb/>removed from the surviving syntype so the discrepancy cannot be resolved.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>However, I am of the opinion that on this occasion a lapsus calami occurred and that Michaelsen<tei:lb/>made a clerical error. His description, and the sole syntype, otherwise match closely the specimens<tei:lb/>from Akoto Ambiente. In any case, the location of the caeca recorded by Michaelsen would be far<tei:lb/>more posterior than is usual among other species where the caecal series commonly begins in or<tei:lb/>nearby segment xxvi. If new material should be discovered with caeca located as described by<tei:lb/>Michaelsen, then clearly the identity of the present series and the relationship with the new material<tei:lb/>will need careful appraisal.</tei:p>

      </tei:div>

         <tei:p>THE EARTHWORM GENUS Millsonia 293</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Millsonia hortensis sp. nov.<tei:lb/>(Figs 5B &amp; 6B)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DIAGNOSIS.          <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 142-252 mm (88 mm regenerating), diameter 4-5 mm.<tei:lb/>Segments 212-272 (111 regenerating); triannulate, caudal region slightly swollen. Male pores paired combined with the<tei:lb/>prostatic pores above setal line b on xvii, each is carried on a porophore and seen as a transverse slit<tei:lb/>with flap-like lips, the posterior lip in particular being more fully developed. Female pores paired<tei:lb/>on xiv where they are located anteriorly to the setal ring between setal lines a and b. Spermathecal<tei:lb/>pores paired in furrow 8/9 in setal line b. Papillae paired on segments viii-x, xvi and xviii nearby or<tei:lb/>slightly above setal line b, each on a raised circular glandular area; raised mid-ventral pads each<tei:lb/>with two, closely paired, papillae in furrows 14/15, 18/19, 20/21, 21/22 and on segment xviii.<tei:lb/>Mid- ventral surface heavily pigmented and glandular between setal lines aa over segments (xxiii,<tei:lb/>xxiv) xxv-xxxii (xxxiii).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Setae closely paired, ventral; post-clitellar formula aa : ab : be : cd = 6 : 1 : 4 : 1 where dd =<tei:lb/>two-thirds of the body circumference.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Internal characters. Septa 4/5-11/12 strongly muscularized. Gizzards highly muscular and<tei:lb/>of equal size. Four to five pairs of intestinal caeca present in xxvi-xxx, the first and/or the last<tei:lb/>pairs may be reduced in either diameter or length. Prostates, single pair highly convoluted lying<tei:lb/>mainly in xviii ectally with a muscular duct that passes forwards into the ventral parietes of xvii.<tei:lb/>Spermathecae paired in ix, duct long and stout with a large distal ampulla, diverticulum multi-<tei:lb/>ocular located midway along the duct; the duct may be convoluted or lead across the segment so<tei:lb/>that the ampulla of the right spermatheca may lie against the lateral parietes of the left side and vice<tei:lb/>versa the ampulla of the left spermatheca lie by the right parietes. Nephridia: meronephridia<tei:lb/>present throughout the body with a single pair of holonephridia additionally present in each<tei:lb/>segment throughout the intestinal region.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>TYPE LOCALITY. Botanic Garden, Aburi, southern Ghana.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MATERIAL EXAMINED. 4C Botanic Garden, Aburi (550'N. 01 1'W.), southern Ghana; coll. J.D. Plisko, date?<tei:lb/>BM(NH) 1984.4.128-131 (syntypes of Millsonia hortensis) .</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DISTRIBUTION. Known only from the type locality.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Millsonia inermis (Michaelsen, 1892)<tei:lb/>(Figs7C&amp;8E)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Benhamia inermis Michaelsen, 1892: 209; Beddard, 1895:568.<tei:lb/>Dichogaster inermis: Michaelsen, 1900: 366; Michaelsen, 1937: 501.<tei:lb/>Dichogaster inermis typica Michaelsen, 1912: 28.<tei:lb/>Millsonia inermis: Omodeo, 1958: 59; Sims, 1965a: 299.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DIAGNOSIS. Spermathecal pores paired by the posterior borders of segments vii and viii ('7/8/9'), in<tei:lb/>adults each pair opens into a median vestibule whereas in subadults they are superificial and<tei:lb/>located slightly above setal line b; male pores paired xviii, prostatic pores paired xvii and xix within<tei:lb/>a deeply invaginated male field; female pores paired within aa about distance \ ab below a and<tei:lb/>somewhat anterior to the setal ring; paired papillae usually present slightly above setal line b by the<tei:lb/>posterior borders of segments ix-xxiii, in subadults additional paired papillae often medially to the<tei:lb/>Spermathecal pores; usually 14 pairs of intestinal caeca present, occasionally less perhaps 1 1 pairs<tei:lb/>(xxviii, xxix) xx-xl (xli, xlii, xliii); meronephric only.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 123-364, diameter 4-1 Omm. Segments 365-384<tei:lb/>(regenerating individuals common but 384 segments in one aclitellate, (?) juvenile 123 mm long),<tei:lb/>mainly triannulate but further subdivision common in the pre-clitellar region. First dorsal pore<tei:lb/>12/13(13/14) occasionally occluded in the clitellar region when the first dorsal pore occurs at the<tei:lb/>posterior border of the clitellum. Clitellum xii-xix, saddle-shaped. Male pores paired xviii dis-<tei:lb/>charging into paired seminal grooves joining the paired prostatic pores in xvii and xix; in fully<tei:lb/>mature specimens the seminal grooves are hidden within a deeply invaginated genital field but in<tei:lb/>subadults the grooves may be seen lying between setal lines b and c. The genital field is encircled<tei:lb/>by a raised rim with a single median anterior papilla and paired posterior papillae, within the<tei:lb/>invagination two pairs of papillae may often be seen lying medially to the seminal grooves. Female<tei:lb/>pores paired xiv within aa about distance \ ab from a located slightly anteriorly to the setal ring.<tei:lb/>Spermathecal pores paired in the hinder regions of segments vii and viii in the anterior walls of<tei:lb/>furrows 7/8/9 about distance ab above setal line b; two pairs of associated papillae commonly<tei:lb/>present on each of segments vii and viii, the first pair are located at the same level as the sperma-<tei:lb/>thecal pores but lie within aa while the second pair are adjacent but located more anteriorly and<tei:lb/>medially. Paired papillae usually present near the posterior borders of most of segments ix-xxii<tei:lb/>(except in the genital field) lying slightly above the setal line b, sometimes the papillae may be<tei:lb/>multiple.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Setae closely paired, ventral; post-clitellar formula aa : ab : be : cd = 5 : 1 : 4 : 1 where dd =<tei:lb/>two-thirds of the body circumference. Setae in the clitellar region often with the setal couples on<tei:lb/>raised genital tumescences.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Internal characters. Septa 4/5-11/12 greatly thickened, 12/13 and 13/14 less so. Gizzards<tei:lb/>strongly muscularized and of equal size. Intestinal caeca 14 pairs present sometimes fewer (11)<tei:lb/>located (xxviii, xxix) xxx-xl (xli-xliii), the posteriormost three pairs are commonly shorter and<tei:lb/>arise more laterally. Prostates paired JCVK and xix highly convoluted with a slender muscular<tei:lb/>portion ectally; the hinder pair are commonly smaller than the anterior pair. Spermathecae paired<tei:lb/>viii and ix, basically digitiform but the distal part may be slightly dilated to form an ampulla-like<tei:lb/>swelling; adiverticulate. Nephridia: only meronephridia present.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>TYPE LOCALITY. Adeli, Togo.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>DIAGNOSIS. Prostates paired, highly<tei:lb/>convoluted in the pre-caecal segments of the anterior intestine from where they lead forward to<tei:lb/>enter the parietal wall of a massive pair of copulatory pouches in xvii that, with full maturity,<tei:lb/>extend into xvi and xviii.          <tei:p>REMARKS. This species forms a couplet with the mainly Ghanian species mima, since the immature<tei:lb/>and (?) subadult individuals of nigra are also large worms with paired Spermathecal and male<tei:lb/>pores and both species have meronephridial excretory systems. However, the adults of nigra are<tei:lb/>separable externally by having a large single mid-ventral male pore and a single Spermathecal<tei:lb/>vestibulum, and internally by the presence of a pair of massive copulatory pouches, while the<tei:lb/>septum of the ovarian segment is muscularized and there are usually more intestinal caeca.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 90-1 82 mm, diameter 4-6 mm. Segments 142-198,<tei:lb/>mainly triannulate but further subdivision common especially in the pre-clitellar region. First<tei:lb/>dorsal pore 5/6. Clitellum xiv-xix, saddle-shaped. Male pores paired xviii (not seen externally)<tei:lb/>discharging into paired, longitudinal seminal grooves joining the (paired) prostatic pores in jcv<tei:lb/>and xix; the seminal grooves are located laterally in an invaginated genital field but, depending on<tei:lb/>the techniques employed to relax, kill, fix and preserve specimens, these may not be seen. The<tei:lb/>genital field is encircled by a raised glandular rim with an anterior and a posterior papilla, the field<tei:lb/>is invaginated with paired spherical to digitiform processes in xvii and xix usually partly lying<tei:lb/>under the external rim, other papillae may also occur. Female pore single, median ventral within<tei:lb/>the setal ring of xiv, usually inconspicuous but occasionally lying within a small transverse fold in<tei:lb/>the body wall. Spermathecal pores paired in furrows 7/8/9 lying across setal lines ab, the body- wall<tei:lb/>in their vicinity (from ? vii-? ix between setal lines cc) may sometimes be slightly raised also with<tei:lb/>one or two randomly arranged papillae. Apart from these papillae and those of the male field, there<tei:lb/>are no other papillae. Sometimes the ventral surface of xiv may be raised between the borders of the<tei:lb/>clitellum when the ventral setae may be carried by genital tumescence, while occasionally the<tei:lb/>ventral surface on xxvi-xxxiii between aa may also be raised slightly.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Setae closely paired, small, ventral couples slightly stouter than the lateral couples; post-clitellar<tei:lb/>formula aa : ab : be : cd = 4 : 1 : 4 : 1 where dd = two-thirds of the body circumference.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Internal characters. Septum 4/5 thickened, 5/6-8/9 membranous, 9/10-12/13 moderately<tei:lb/>thickened. Gizzards each with a proventricular-like anterior region and a highly muscular<tei:lb/>posterior region; both large and displaced posteriorly with the hinder gizzards lying within the<tei:lb/>parietes of ix and jc. Intestinal caeca, 13-1 7 pairs present, usually 14 pairs full-size, (xxvii) xxviii-xli<tei:lb/>(xlii, xliii). Prostates paired xvii and xix, each is highly convoluted with slender muscular portion<tei:lb/>ectally. Spermathecae paired viii and ix, in mature individuals the basal region of the duct has a<tei:lb/>granular appearance while distally the ampulla becomes bipartite; adiverticulate. Nephridia: only<tei:lb/>meronephridia present.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>REMARKS. The species is named in honour of Professor Joseph J. Niles of the University of the West<tei:lb/>Indies, Georgetown, Guyana, in recognition of his interest in the earthworms of the Kumasi area<tei:lb/>when he was a member of the staff at Prempeh College and later when that institution became the<tei:lb/>University of Science and Technology, Kumasi.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Millsonia nota sp. nov.<tei:lb/>(Figs 5A &amp; 6A)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DIAGNOSIS.          <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 56-72 mm, diameter 2-3 mm. Segments 179-210. First<tei:lb/>dorsal pore in furrow 8/9. Clitellum xiii-xvii, saddle-shaped. Female pores paired in the setal ring on xiv, inconspicuous, they lie<tei:lb/>within aa about the distance ab below a. Spermathecal pores paired in furrow 8/9 in setal line b.<tei:lb/>Papillae paired in furrows 10/1 1/12/13/14 by setal line b; a single mid- ventral papilla is present in<tei:lb/>furrow 28/29 in one syntype.          <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 140- 170 mm, diameter 4-5 mm. Segments 226-301,<tei:lb/>multiannulate. First dorsal pore 6/7. Clitellum ^xiii-xviii, saddle-shaped. Female pores<tei:lb/>paired in setal line a, slightly anterior to the setal ring. Spermathecal pores paired in furrows 7/8/9<tei:lb/>in setal line b. Numerous papillae are irregularly arranged in clusters over setal lines ab on the<tei:lb/>hinder surfaces of some or all of segments vi, vii and viii; paired papillae present within setal lines aa<tei:lb/>in furrows 10/1 1-22/23 often becoming segmental behind the clitellum when they may extend back<tei:lb/>as far as to segment xxv.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Setae stated to be the same as in M. anomala (i.e. small, closely paired, ventral; post-clitellar<tei:lb/>formula aa : ab : be : cd = 14:1-2:9:1 where dd = three-quarters of the body circumference).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Internal characters. First septum 4/5, septa 5/6/7 greatly thickened, septa 7/8/9/10 less so.<tei:lb/>Gizzard highly muscularized in segment vi (no information is available on the condition of the<tei:lb/>oesophagus in segment v, whether the oesophageal wall is slightly thickened as in M. anomala was<tei:lb/>not made clear by Omodeo &amp; Vaillaud). Intestinal caeca, seven pairs present xxvi-xxxii. Prostates<tei:lb/>paired xvii and xix. Spermathecae paired viii and ix, adiverticulate, very long, slenger, uniform<tei:lb/>without any differentiation into ampulla and duct (? immature). Nephridia: meronephridia occur<tei:lb/>throughout the body, additionally each post-clitellar segment contains a pair of holonephridia.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>TYPE LOCALITY. Vicinity of Gpakobo and Singrobo, southeastern Ivory Coast.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>RECORDS. 4C (? subadults) Sandy soil in savannah between Gpakobo and Singrobo (15 km SE of Lamto,<tei:lb/>613'N. 502'W.), southeastern Ivory Coast; (syntypes of Millsonia omodeoi, Station d'Ecologie Tropicale de<tei:lb/>Lamto as Millsonia anomala forma leptocystis Omodeo &amp; Vaillaud, 1967).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DISTRIBUTION. Southeastern Ivory Coast.</tei:p>

However, under Article 16 of the</tei:p>

         <tei:p>International Code of Zoological Nomenclature (3rd edition 1985) a scientific name proposed with<tei:lb/>the term 'variety' or 'form' after 1960 is infrasubspecific and excluded from nomenclature, thus the<tei:lb/>epithet leptocystis proposed for the 'nouvelle forme' by Omodeo and Vaillaud is not an available<tei:lb/>name. It is necessary, therefore, to provide a name for this species which I do in honour of Professor<tei:lb/>P. Omodeo.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>Notes on two new species of the genus Agastrodrilus (Octochaetidae) from Ghana</tei:p>
         <tei:p>The genus Agastrodrilus was erected by Omodeo and Vaillaud (1967) to accommodate two new<tei:lb/>earthworms from the Ivory Coast that differed from species of the genus Millsonia in the reduced</tei:p>
         <tei:pb/>
      </tei:div>
      <tei:div>
         <tei:p>THE EARTHWORM GENUS Millsonia</tei:p>
         <tei:p>309</tei:p>
         <tei:p>sizes of the gizzards, an increase in the length of the clitellum and the large size of the ventral setae.<tei:lb/>Subsequently, Lavelle (1981) described a third species but with a clitellum extending over only<tei:lb/>segments xiii-xix (like the clitella of many species of Millsonia), but more importantly he reported<tei:lb/>predation on other small species of earthworms. He observed one individual feeding on Stuhl-<tei:lb/>manniaporifera (Eudrilidae) by entwining itself around the worm and swallowing it head-first, like<tei:lb/>a boa constrictor consuming its prey. His observations led him to assess the adaptive significance of<tei:lb/>the characters of the genus. The reduction in the size and weak musculature of the gizzards and the<tei:lb/>absence of a typhlosole, he interpreted as adaptations to a carnivorous diet; while the large size of<tei:lb/>the ventral setae was regarded as important in the capture and retention of the prey. These three<tei:lb/>species were described from the wet savannahs of the Ivory Coast, but specimens which prove to<tei:lb/>represent two new species have been found from the forested country of southern Ghana among<tei:lb/>material of Millsonia reported above.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Genus AGASTRODRILUS Omodeo and Vaillaud, 1967<tei:lb/>Agastrodrilus Omodeo &amp; Vaillaud, 1967:925.<tei:lb/>TYPE SPECIES. Agastrodrilus opisthogynus Omodeo and Vaillaud, 1967 (new designation).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DIAGNOSIS. Octochaetidae lacking penial setae; ventral setae (ab) large, at least in the pre-clitellar<tei:lb/>region; two simple rudimentary gizzards present in segments v and v/; lamellate calciferous glands<tei:lb/>paired on the oesophagus in segments xv, xvi and xvii; paired digitate intestinal caeca, one pair in<tei:lb/>each of several contiguous segments, present on the anterior intestine; typhlosole absent.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DISTRIBUTION. Ivory Coast and southern Ghana.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REMARKS. Members of this genus are remarkable not only because of their predatory behaviour<tei:lb/>but also morphologically in the case of three of the species since the locations of their reproductive<tei:lb/>systems and pores differ from those in other Octochaetidae. The two new species from Ghana<tei:lb/>described below are readily separable from the representatives of Agastrodrilus known from the<tei:lb/>Ivory Coast by, among other characters, the smaller number of intestinal caeca while insolitus<tei:lb/>sp.nov. also has the spermathecal pores situated in furrow 7/8 (see Table 2).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Table 2 Distinguishing characters of species of the genus Agastrodrilus</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Agastrodrilus insolitus sp. nov.<tei:lb/>(FigsllA&amp;12A)</tei:p>

Spermathecal pores paired in furrow 7/8 in setal line b; combined male and prostatic<tei:lb/>pores paired on segment jcvm female pores paired xiv within seta lines aa, lying in the setal ring<tei:lb/>approximately distance ab from a; paired papillae on a single, transversely oval, mid- ventral pad</tei:p>

         <tei:p>a<tei:lb/>1</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Fig. 11 Agastrodrilus spp. anterior region, ventral view (not to scale). (A)insolitus; (K)lavellei.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>present in most furrows between the spermathecal and male pores; anteriorly setae ab greatly<tei:lb/>enlarged especially on segments v, vi and vii; five pairs of intestinal caeca xxvi-xxx; meronephric<tei:lb/>only.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 71-1 10 mm, diameter 2-5-3-5 mm. Segments 126-249.<tei:lb/>First dorsal pore in furrow 9/10. Clitellum xiii-\ xix, saddle-shaped. Male pores paired united with<tei:lb/>the prostatic pores jcvm slightly above setal line b, each located on a low porophore. Female pores<tei:lb/>paired in the setal ring of xiv within setal lines aa, each located about distance ab from a thus lying a<tei:lb/>little more than distance ab part. Spermathecal pores paired 7/8 in setal line b. Papillae paired in<tei:lb/>furrows 10/1 1-16/17 within aa, each pair on a raised oval pad extending above setal lines b; raised<tei:lb/>pads occasionally present within the ventral setae on segments xx, xxi.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Setae ab becoming progressively enlarged until long and stout on segments v, vi, vii and at the<tei:lb/>same time becoming more distant with the setal formula of aa : ab : be : cd = 5 : 4 : 7 : 1 on vii,<tei:lb/>whereas setae cd on the same segments are small or absent; behind the clitellum setae small and<tei:lb/>uniform with the setal formula aa : ab : be : cd = 9 : 1 : 7 : 1 where dd is three-quarters to three-<tei:lb/>fifths the body circumference.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Internal characters. Septa 4/5-9/10 strongly thickened, 10/11 and 11/12 less so. Gizzards small,<tei:lb/>weakly muscularized. Intestinal caeca five pairs xxvi-xxx. Prostates single pair, very long and<tei:lb/>convoluted passing through several segments, ectally becoming muscular and passing into the<tei:lb/>parietes in xix. Single pair of spermathecae discharging posteriorly in vii, each somewhat<tei:lb/>T-shaped. The duct, or lower, vertical limb of the 'T', is broad with a lateral diverticulum contain-<tei:lb/>ing a system of branching ducts (more dendritic than racemose), while the ampulla representing the<tei:lb/>upper, horizontal portion of the T', has a long, main (medial) chamber and a small, subsidiary<tei:lb/>(lateral) chamber. Nephridia: meronephridia only present.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>TYPE LOCALITY. Ada Kanyanga, southeastern Ghana.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MATERIAL EXAMINED. 1 8C Soil under tomato plants, Ada Kanyanga (555'N. 005'W.), S.E. Ghana; coll. J.D.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Plisko, date? BM(NH) 1984.4.27-45 (syntypes of Agastrodrilus insolitus).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>4C Cultivated field, Ada Koloidaw (540'N. 025'W.), S.E. Ghana; coll. J.D. Plisko, date? BM(NH)</tei:p>

         <tei:p>2C By a ditch, sugar cane plantations, Kpong (61 1'N. 009'E.), S.E. Ghana; coll. J.D. Plisko, date? BM(NH)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>1984.4.46-47.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DISTRIBUTION. S.E. Ghana.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Agastrodrilus lavellei sp. nov.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>(FigsllB&amp;12B)<tei:lb/>DIAGNOSIS. Spermathecal pores paired in furrow 8/9 within setal lines ab; combined male and</tei:p>

         <tei:p>THE EARTHWORM GENUS Millsonia 3 1 1</tei:p>
         <tei:p>A B</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Fig. 12 Spermathecae (not to scale) of Agastrodrilus spp. (A.)insolitus; (S)lavellei.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>prostatic pores paired xvii; female pores paired xiv slightly anteriorly to the setal ring within setal<tei:lb/>lines aa about ^ aa apart; paired papillae on a single, transversely oval, mid-ventral pad in two<tei:lb/>pre-clitellar and a further two clitellar furrows; setae ab greatly enlarged in the pre-clitellar region,<tei:lb/>eight pairs of intestinal caeca xxiv-xxxi; meronephric only.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DESCRIPTION. External characters. Length 80-132 mm. diameter 2-5-3-0 mm. Segments 216-289,<tei:lb/>multiannulate in the pre-clitellar segments, (up to nine annuli per segment) commonly only tri-<tei:lb/>annulate in the post-clitellar segments. First dorsal pore (9/10) 10/11. Clitellum | xiii-^ xvii,<tei:lb/>saddle-shaped. Male pores paired on xvii in setal line b. Female pores paired on xiv slightly anterior<tei:lb/>to the setal ring within setal lines aa about ^ aa apart. Spermathecal pores paired in furrow 8/9<tei:lb/>located between setal lines ab. Paired papillae immediately within setal lines aa in furrows 10/11,<tei:lb/>11/12, 14/15 and 15/16, each pair on a raised, transversely oval pad lying ventrally between bb,<tei:lb/>other papillae in the genital field (16/17, 17/18, 18/19) are similarly located nearly aa apart but the<tei:lb/>furrows are obliterated and an additional pair occur at bb on xviii. The genital field is usually seen<tei:lb/>as a raised scutate, glandular area, but in older individuals it may become invaginated. A further<tei:lb/>raised, glandular pad may occur ventrally between setae bb on segment xx and sometimes encroach<tei:lb/>onto the adjacent segments.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Setae in the pre-clitellar segments somewhat widely paired where ab are long and stout with the<tei:lb/>setal formula on segment ix being aa : ab : be : cd = 3:2:3:1; post-clitellar setae closely paired,<tei:lb/>small and uniform, setal formula aa : ab : be : cd = 6 : 1 :4 : 1 where ^approximates to two-thirds<tei:lb/>of the body circumference.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Internal characters. Septa 4/5-10/1 1 strongly thickened, 1 1/12 and 12/13 less so. Gizzards small,<tei:lb/>weakly muscularized. Intestinal caeca eight pairs located xxiv-xxxi. Prostates paired, tubular,<tei:lb/>long and convoluted extending through several segments, ectally with a long, muscular duct that<tei:lb/>enters the ventral parietes in xvii. Single pair of spermathecae in ix discharge anteriorly into furrow<tei:lb/>8/9; proximally each has a rotund, globular duct bearing a small ectal multilocular diverticulum<tei:lb/>and distally there is a wrinkled, duct-like ampulla with a diameter about one-third that of the<tei:lb/>duct. Circular, flask-like pads are present in the parietal wall internally to the external papillae.<tei:lb/>Nephridia: meronephridia only present.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>TYPE LOCALITY. Near Achimota, Ghana.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>MATERIAL EXAMINED. 13C Bush near Achimota, S.E. Ghana; coll. J.D. Plisko, date? ; BM(NH)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>1984.4.456-467 (syntypes of Agastrodrilus lavallei).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>4C Bush near Achimota, S.E. Ghana; coll. J.D. Plisko, date ? ; BM(NH) 1984.4.468^71.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>5C 1 A Green Hill, Legon, Achimota, S.E. Ghana; coll. J.D. Plisko 26 Jun 1965; BM(NH) 1984.4.473-478.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>1C 'S.E. Ghana'; coll. J.D. Plisko, date ?; BM(NH) 1984.4.472.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>1C Bodonya, New Achimota Village, S.E. Ghana; coll. J.J. Niles, date ?; BM(NH) 1968.2.30</tei:p>
         <tei:p>DISTRIBUTION. Around Achimota (535'N. 015'E.), S.E. Ghana.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>REMARKS. The species is named in honour of Dr Patrick Lavelle in recognition of his important<tei:lb/>contributions to the study of the ecology of the earthworms of western Africa.</tei:p>

         <tei:p>British Museum (Natural History)</tei:p>
         <tei:p>A monograph on the Poly clad Turbellaria</tei:p>
         <tei:p>S. Prudhoe</tei:p>
         <tei:p>This is the first comprehensive monograph of the polyclad turbellarians (free-living marine</tei:p>
         <tei:p>flatworms) to be published since 1884. It consists of a general account of the structure, natural</tei:p>
         <tei:p>history, classification and techniques of study, a detailed illustrated review of the families and</tei:p>
         <tei:p>genera, and comprehensive bibliographies and indices. It will be an essential reference work for</tei:p>
         <tei:p>marine biologists worldwide.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>1985, 240pp (approx), 140 figs. Hardback. 19 8585187 37-50.</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Co-published with Oxford University Press.</tei:p>
         <tei:pb/>
      </tei:div>

         <tei:p>A review of the genus Hydrocynus Cuvier, 1819 (Teleostei: Characiformes).</tei:p>
         <tei:p>By B. Brewster</tei:p>
         <tei:p>A taxonomic revision of the southern Arabian Enidae sensu lato (Mollusca:<tei:lb/>Pulmonata). By P. B. Mordan</tei:p>
         <tei:p>Revision of western African earthworm genus Millsonia (Octochaetidae:<tei:lb/>Oligochaeta). By R. W. Sims</tei:p>
